12 December, 1968
Subject: LIRING/3 Receipt of Letter from Gustavo Colindrés.
=
1. LIRING/3 reportedto Rowton at 1700 on 12/42/68 that he had received
a letter from Gustavo Colindres, a Guatemalan of about 40 years age
whom he had met in the Pavón prison in Guatemala City. LIRING/3 stated
that Colindres is the uncle (mother's side) of the León Barrios brothers,
although he does not have the same name of sra. Barrios. L/3 explained
that they were born of different fathers. L/3 added that Colindres was
imprisoned some 18 months ago for responsibility in an arms cache dis-
covered in or near his home.
2. The following is Rowton's translation of the original letter which
ZIRINC/3 gave Rowton for copying:
...
"I hope that when you arrived in your Mexico, you found only peace
and satisfaction in being once again in the warmth of your home.
Here on the farm we have missed you and felt badiy at not bearing
from the artist and the professor, and now that I have succesded in
obtaining your address, I am taking the liberty of dropping your a
few lines. I want you both to keep abreast of what's going on at
the old farm, even though we're still struggling to turn it over to
new owners, but they haven't as yet agreed to the price. I guess
I'll be the last to leave the ship, since I haven't a chance to get
off. The lions are the next to leave their cage.'Lorenzana' left
a month ago and the Queen left on the 2nd of December. Promise me
that when you take a drink you'll toast the farm and the date that
His approaching.
My best to your wife, kisses to your child and my best wishes for
1. your welfare. May this year of strange experiences engrave in your
_ mind the memory of a friend.
/s/ G.Colindres
Guat. 7/12/68
I
Please send your correspondence to me in the name of my wife,Isabel
Donis de Colindres, 5 av. y 7a Calle,lote 6-Manzana 26, Colonia Santa
Marta, Zona 19, Guat. Cuidad, América Central. Men of the inespe
in not court.
3. LIRING/3 told Rowton he understood the "lions are next to leave their
cage" to mean that the León Barrios brothers are soon to be released and
that this letter is a signal to him to be on the alert for a contact fron
them in the near future. L/3 told Howton that he intended to reply to this
1

1.
Forwarded herewith is one copy each for Headquarters
and the Guatemala City Station of the report covering the
debriefing by Wallace B. ROWTON of LIRING-3 on his imprisonment
in Guatemala. Identity A of ROWTON's report is a Guatemalan
rebel living in Mexico who, as addressees will remember. I
accidentally shot himself 111 the ieg a new days prior to his
departure for Guatemala with LIRING-3. This wound may have
convinced the Guatemalans that he had recently been involved
in terrorist activities and may, in fact, have cost him his
life. Identity B of the same report is the nephew of Identity F,
a Mexican Communist who was arrested on 19 September 1968
during a student demonstration in Mexico City; he is still in
jail.
1
2.
As this dispatch is being written, LIRING-3 has an
appointment to talk at length about his experience in Guatemala
with the LIRING Station Chief, LIRING-10. The general idea
is for LIRING-3 to go to PBRUMEN in the hope that he can be
used to penetrate PBRUMEN-sponsored subversion efforts in Latin
America or become, at least for a time, a reporting source in
PBRUMEN.
3. ROWTON and the undersigned are prepared to travel to
Guatemala to discuss the LIRING-3 case and its Guatemalan/FAR
implications whenever the Guatemala City Station, after
reviewing the available information, feels ready for such
discussiou. Please advise.

Director de SIEMPRE!
Hace unos días voíví a la ciudad de México, después de '
haber permanecido encarcelado Jurante ccs) 7 meses en !
Guatemala, sujeto a un juicio del cuci sal absuelto- acu-
sado por las autoridades de aquel país de "atentar contra
las instituciones democráticas".
No pretendo hacer una crónica de les circunstancias de
mi detención, del proceso judicici, etc., pues estos detalles
en parte fueron dados a conocer en su oportunidad por SIEM-
PRE!; pero sí quisera relatale en una forma breve algunas
de las cosas que o cervé durante esos meses en el campo'
de concentración de Pavón, mai llamado "Granjo Penal Pa-!
vón”, donde estuve confinado.
f
Dicha "granja" está situada a más o menos 23 Kms. de
la ciudad de Guatemala en el Departamento de Frajanes Y:
consiste en un hoyco artificial rodeado de cercar electrifi
cedes ♥ taroles de vixilancia mmn si ''ne of
concentración nomis. So supone que en los paises civilizados
los sistemas carcelarios disponen de los medios suficientes para proporcionar a los reciu-
sos un mínimo de comodidades o elementos que le permitan su desarrollo o rehabilita-
ción; pero en este sitio sólo imperan el terror y el hambre, así como las condiciones más
infrañumanas y expeluznantes, ya que la insalubridad y la falta de atención en todos los
aspectos es lo que alí impera
La población aproximada de "la Granja" cocila entre 1,300 y 1,500 reca, de los cua
les los "presos políticos" no Legan a 20, ya que les detenidos por delitos de esta natura
leza son generalmente asesinados después de su detención y estar sujetos a tortures.
}
Por lo tanto, ia casi totalidad de los presos son "delincuentes comunes", pero podría
decirse que en un 40% son. inocentes del delito de que se les acusa: Dues en Guatemala.
para ser encarcelado no es necesario tener pruebas en contra. Una simple acusación po
Ecíaca o de particulares basta para quedar sujeto a un proceso en el cual es común sat
fir absuelto después de uno o dos años de encarcelamiento.
La administración interna del penal está encomendada a los reclusos, para ic cual
so escoge a los delincuentes más depravados y que tienen condenas jargas asesinos, dro!.
gudicios, etc.
Para mantener la disciplina se ha formado un cuerpo de represión denominado "ser:
vicio especial" o "garroteros", como vulvormente se les ilaman. Este grupo, cuya impuni
dad es ilimitada, mantiene a los reclusos terror constante, ya que basta la falta más
mínima para que golpeen con saña brutal c. infractor, llegándole a causar hasta la muer
te.
El penal no proporciona a los reciusos ningún medio de trabajo, pero si propicia la
formación de matias internas que explotan a quienes tienen mayores necesidades, hacién
dolos trabajar en fábricas elementales de algunas artesanics: canustos, juguetes rudiment
tarios o pelotas de futbol; productos que envian a la calle para su venta y de los cua
les esas mañas obtienen grandes ganancias que comparten con la dirección del Penal.
Uno de los negocios más productivos, y del cual participan las autoridades en com-
binación con los reclusos influyentes, es la venta de seconales sódicos y manquanc a los
reclusos; drogas con las que una gran mayoria trata de borrar su desesperanón y anguṣ-
ticz, pero trayendo por consecuencia reyertas que degeneran muchas veces en es asesinato.
Como mencioné antes, la "Granja Penal ce Pavón" consiste en un hoyarico artifician
cuyo españo habitable se reduce a un rectángulo de 170 por 70 metros, aproximadamen-
te, el cual incluye 5 cuadras y una explanada al aire libre, irónicamente amada "or 1-
po deportivo”. Cada una de las cuadras alberga un promedio de 250 persones que viven
la más absoluta promiscuidad. Para agravar esta situación funciona dianafiente ---du-
rante 12 horas- un altoparlante, aucuble en todos los rincones, y que se ubiza para
- acrecentar el amedrentamiento y el terror. Por ese altoparlante se Mama a as recluidos,
que son solicitados para presentarse a la autoridad del penal, pero siempre bojciendo hin-
capié en la amenaza y en ia intimidación.
Los reincidentes o reos peligrosos, están confinados en el Triánguio", que es un
espacio pequeño, protegido por alambradas, del cual no pueden salır ni siquiera a la ex
planada. En las cuadras, sólo una parte de les reclusos dispone de literas; (Sa mayoric
duerme en el suelo cubriéndose con trapos nees o cartones. La cimentación; que el pe.
nal proporciona consiste en dos pequeños panes y caté por la mañana a tortilles y un

27 NR 18029!
A
1. BECAUSE LIRING-3 COULD NOT LOGICALLY HAVE GAINED DETAILED
INSIGHT INTO INSURGENCY MOVEMENT IN GUATEMALA DURING ENCARCERATION,
DO NOT BELIEVE IT NECESSARY FOR GUATEMALA CITY STATION OFFICÉR
PROVIDE EXTENSIVE AND DETAILED BRIEFING FOR PREPARATION LIRING-3
REPORT. SUGGEST FOLLOWING GENERAL GUIDELINES, SUBJECT TO HQS
APPROVAL, WHICH OSTENSIBILY TO BE IMPRESSIONS OF LIRING-3 BASED
ON CONVERSATIONS WITH FAR LEADERS WHILE IN JAIL.
A. EMPHASIZE FRAGMENTATION, DISORGANIZATION AND COMPETITION
OF INSURGENT FORCES HAVE SERIOUSLY DISRUPTED INSURGENT MOVEMENT,

SHOULD BE CANDID WITH LIRING/10 AND TELL HIM WHAT AND AS MUCH AS HE

15. Subject was born in Mexico City in 1930 of middle class family.
Subject's grandfather was a well-known textile merchant who served some 12
years as president of the Chamber of Commerce. At least one of Subject's
aunts is currently well-to-do and the owner of several 30artment houses in
Mexico City. Subject has at present little or no contact with his family.

0 PRPUMEN: Activities of LIRING-3, LIRING-4 May through Mid-September 1968
ACTION REQUIRED - REFERENCES
201-378882
REF:
HMMA 34682, 17 May 1968
MICROFILMED
OCT 17 1968
Action Required: For your information.
DOC. MICRO. SER.
1. Forwarded under separate cover are twelve reports prepared by
Wallace B. ROWION on the activities of LIRING-3, LIRING-4, and contacts of
the latter.
2. The main topic covered in ROWTON's reports is LIRING-4's efforts to
obtain help in getting LIRING-3 out of jail in Guatemale as soon as possible.
LIRING-4 is almost penniless (REWTON has made only token payments to her
after 15 June) and has been moving from one apartment to a cheaper one living
on the sale of paintings left by LIRING-3 and small loans from leftist contacts.
In the hope that she may be able to do something for 1TRING-3, LIRING-4 has
resisted all of ROWTON's efforts to get her to undertake a clandestine mission
to PBRUMEN, a mission, as Headquarters knows, was plaaned long agɔ. As a
foreigner, LIRING-4 cannot work in Mexico without taking the chance of being
deported, if caught. Although she has not tried it, she would probably be
refused a visa to go to Guatemala to visit LIRING-3. She might also face
difficulties in Guatemala including possible detention and interrogation if
she succeeded in obtaining an entry permit to that country.
1
3. By mid-September 1968 LIEINC-4 had received very little help from
her Mexican leftist or outright Communist friends. In spite of promises to

7. Contacts between ROSTON and LIRING-4 have taken place with decreasing
frequency because the usefulness of LIRING-4 to WOFIRM has sharply decreased
and because LIRING-4 is more and more convinced that ROWTON cannot or will
not help her obtain the release of LIRING-3. In her frantic efforts to do
something for LIRING-3, LIRING-4 has in fact not had any contact with ROWTON
since early September. Unless LIRING-3 is released by the Guatemalan
authorities or receives only a light sentence keeping him in jail only a short
time longer, it is doubtful that LIRING-4 will be of much use to POSTON and
the Station.

12 June, 1968
NA LACE B. kowton Meeting with LIZING/4.
1. Rowton met with IRING/4 at the Diana Restaurant, Calle Mississippi,
from 1300 until about 1410 on 11 June, 1968. LIRING/4 reported that the
had finally moved into the apartment in the Edificio Condesa with the
few pieces of furniture of the Tacubaya apartment. She stated that she
intended to remain in close touch with her friend Blanca Peña de Anand
and, of course, Catalina Cepero, at whose homes she hoped to be able to
take her main meals. DIAING/4 added that she was still attmepting to
find some sort of work to help her meet her expenses, as well as to find
a person, preferably a student, to rent a room in her apartment.
2. With regard to amplement TYSTIC/ stated that LTRTNG/2 had told her
the previous week that his recommendation that she been employed in the
(outside) LIKING cultural office had been turned down and consequently
she had appealed to Mexican friends to help her find employment. She
also told Rowton that she had queried LIRING/2 about FBAUMEN students who
might share her apartment but was told that the only female students (two)
at present in Mexico were studying in Fátzcuaro.
nala
3. LIRING/4 continued that she had been receiving letters regularly from
LIRING/3 directly from his place of confinement. She showed Rowton a por-
tion of one of the letters in which LIRING/3 stated that there were about
2,000 prisoners in all and that he feels obliged to share whatever food
he can purchase with the money sent to him by DIRING/4 with six others who
are closest to him and whose relatives cannot provide even the essentials
of a basic diet. According to LIRING/4, LINING/3 has not complained about
what appear to be very difficult conditions but has revealed his constant
fear of physical violence, the threat of which he feels hangs over the
prison. LIMING/4 told howton that she had finally obtained officially no-
tarized statements from the proper Mexican authorities testifying to LI-
RING/3's bona fides as an artist, as requested by the Nexican Consul. She
gave Howton a letter from the latter which requests this information(copy
of which is attached)..
4. LIRING/4, in reply to Rowton's queries, stated that she still hoped to
be able to make the trip to FBRUMEN but could not consider leaving Nexico
at this time in view of LIRING/3's situation and the fact that she was the
only point of contact he had on the outside. Rowton sympathized with her
but stressed that his ability to help her financially was limited by her

Wallace B. kowton Recontact with RODOLFO REYES.
1. Rowton met Rodolfo Reyes at about 2230 in the dining room of the
Vendimia Restaurant and night club (60 calle Liverpool) by design on
15 July, 1968. Rowton had previously been informed by LIRING/11 that
Reyes was currently working at the Vendimia and felt that he should
meet Reyes again to pass along the story that he had given to LIRING/11
that he was unable to locate LIRING/3 or LIRING/4 in the hope that Reyes
would disclose LIRING/3's arrest.
2. As soon as Rowton met Reyes the latter invited him to a corner table
to a
with what appeared to be superficial cordiality. He asked howton how be
had located him and appeared a little surprised when Rowton said that
LIRING/11 had given him hthename of the night club and the address. Rowton
then alleged that he had been away for the past three months in Switzerland
and Canada and just the previous week in Monterrey and Nuevo Laredo trying
to buy a car (Rowton had given the same story to LIRING/11). Rowton continueć
that when he returned he had been unable to locate LIRING/3 or his wife and
that they had not replied to his letters from Europe.
3. Reyes then revealed that LIRING/3 had been arrested in Guatemala and
charged with the murder of three men! Rowton feigned surprise, shock and
fear at this news. He told Reyes that this might have serious consequences
for his commercial contacts, whose names LIRING/3 might reveal as well as
for himself. Reyes then said he thought LIRING/3 was very stupid to get
himself arrested in such a country where anything can happen inside as well
as outside of jail. In reply to Rowton's query Reyes stated that LIRING/4
was probably in PBRUMEN.
4. When Rowton remarked that he could not believe that LIRING/11 had refused
to tell him the news about LIRING/3, Reyes replied that it was quite possible
that LIRING/11 did not know about it, especially since he, Reyes, had just
leanred about it some three days previously. At this point the conversation
was interrupted by the arrival at the table of a negro choreographer and
his (white) Mexican wife,who appeared to be close friends of Reyes. Rowton
sat with them through the floorshow and in the course ɗ conversation Howton
discovered that the negro was a Cuban who had emigrated to Mexico some
fifteen years previously. Neither he nor his wife appeared to be interested
in politics. They both seemed dedicated to his career Bellas Artes.

maining

por las autoridades guate-

en defensa de estos infor-
tunados compatriotas, pero
hasta ahora sus gestiones
oficiales no han sido aten-

gobierno de Guatemala.

publicamos copia de la car-

manos de la ONU:

ONU.
Por este medic nos diri-
gimos a ustedes, pidiendo-

tro caso.
El día 13 de abril de
1968, mientras nos dirigía-
mos pacíficamente a la Re-
pública del Salvador y Hon-
dūras, fuimos detenidos con
lup de violencia por ele.
mentos del Ejército de Gua-
temala, en un lugar llame-
do "El Cable” a cuatro ki-
lómetros escasamente de la
frontera de México con
Guatemala denominada "La
Mesilla".
De ahí, llevados a un lu-
gar llamado "Buenos Ai-
res
donde permanecimos
por una noche sujetos a tor.
tures fisicas y morales. Al
dia siguiente fuimos condu-
cidos en un avión (No. 540)
de la FAG a la ciudad capt
tal, donde quedamos encar-
celados en el 20. Cuerpo de
la Policía Nacional, sujetos
también a torturas físicas y
morales que hicieron vha.
can poligrar nuestra vida.
Tan obvio es el error co-
metido con nosotros, que a
pesar de que nuestra de-
tención se llevó a cabo des-
de el dia 13 de abril, como
puede ser probedo fácil
mente con testigos presen-
ciales y desde entonces
mantenidos en prisión, el
gobierno guatemalteco nos
acusa de haber sido deteni-
dos el día 17 del mismo
mes, en las calles de la ciu-
dad. Repartiendo propa-
ganda subversiva!! Incon-
gruencia mayor no cabe en
ninguna mente que se pre-
cie de normal.
Desde el día 26 de abril
de 1968 fuimos confinados
al campo de concentración
de Pavón, mal llamado
"Granja Penal". Donde las
condiciones de vida para
los reclusos y la violencia
al que están sometidos, son
espeluznantes como puede
ser fácilmente comprobado
por la H. Comisión de los
Derechos Humanos.
Hemos sido sujetos a un
"juicio" que el gobierno
guatemalteco alarga delibe.
adamente con el único pro-
pácito de rukeisje
a la vez perjudicarnos; por
esto y sobre todo por con
siderar en grave peligro
nuestra integridad fisica,
pedimos la rápida interven.
ción de la H. Comisión de
los Derechos Humanos pa-
ra que se exija nuestra in-
mediata libertad.
Atentamente, Cárcel de
Pavón, Guatemala, Julio 68.

10 December, 1963
LIRING/3 Report of Contact with Humberto González Vega.
+
1. At 1000 on 9/12/68 at Identity A · LIRING/3 reported to Rowton.
that he had met with Humberto González Vega on 5 and 6 December. He re-
lated that he had gone back to the apartment on Calle Manzanillo on the
afternoon of 5 December, met González and made a date to see him again
on the morning of 6 December. When he returned about 1030 on that day
González' wife said that he had just stepped out to telephone the embassy
of Ecuador. L/3 went out and found González at a nearby telephone booth
and managed to have a relatively detailed chat with him.
2. According to L/3, González sarted off by saying that he had been looking
forward to meeting L/3 for some time, since he had heard a great deal about
him from mutual friends. González went on to say that although he had been
away from Guatemala for the past four years, he kept in touch with his
friends there. He dropped the names of Sandoval Alegría, Jorge Torrón and
a certain Avecillas (phon) who he assumed were known to LIRING/3. He con-
cluded his introductory remarks with the statement that he hoped be and
L/3 would become friends, since they could be of mutual help.
3. González added that he was making a living selling books and was planning
to open a book store at the University. He indicated that he might be able
to help L/3 financially if the latter were interested in this business ven-
.
-
ture. González then stated that he was aware of L/3's arrest and detention
and alleged that he had advance information concerning L/3's trip to Guate-
mala in the company of
Identity D
He then asked L/3 whether
he knew the real purpose of Iden D trip. When L/3 replied in a non-committal
way, González alleged thatIden Dhad been accused of misappropriation of funds:
and took the trip in the hope of defendi..g himself against these charges,
González then produced a typewritten letter, undated and addressed to himself
and signed by "Cruz", advising him of the charges againstIden D. González
told L/3 that the letter was from FAR headquarters and was received some time
beforeIden Dand L/3 left on their trip.
4. González then went on to say that he and his friends were not at all certain
thatiden Dhad been executed, as L/3 and many other people assumed. He stated
that some months ago Iden D mother in Mexico City had received a letter from
him informing her that he was then at Salamá (phon). González added that it
was not to be excluded thatIden Dhad made some sort of deal with the authoritie:
to save his skin in exchange for services he might perform against Far in the
future.
5. González then cautioned L/3 against indiscriminate contacts with persons ·

representing themselves to be from legitimate "revolutionary" movements.
González recounted that he himself had to go into hiding for the previous
two months as a result of his having been exposed to a certain Nuñez who
had arrived in Mexico City with a group of Guatemalan exiles. González des-
cribed Muñez as a known member of the "Mano Blanca" and a former police
officer ("tercero jefe de la Judicial").
i
6. González then asked L/3 whether he had made any close friends while in
Guatemala. This, 4/3 felt,was an attempt to smoke out his relationship with
the Barrios brothers ( Miguel and Juán Beón Barrios). He told nowton that be
evaded the issue by giving a vague reply, to which González replied: "Well,
I hope to have a great surprise for you soon ('alegría')" González then
suggested that they meet again on 12 December and promised to visit L/3 at
his home in the company of his wife, "so that 1/3's and his wife could keep
each other company while they themselves were talking in L/3's apartment."
L/3 told Rowton that he shot this idea down by explaining that although his
wife was revolutionary and trustworthy, he preferred to keep any politicial
discussions strictly between himself and González. The latter, then suggested
that he simply drop by L/3's house and that they both proceed somewhere for
a coffee on a suitable pretext.
__
7. LIRING/3 described Humberto González Vega as a "rather tall"man (about 1.78)
heavy (about 85-90 k.), apparent age 42, with light eyes ("ojos claros") and
straight ("lacio") black hair. He drew Rowton the attached sketch for possible
identification.
8. IIRING/3 agreed with Rowton that it was advisable for him to tell LIRING/9
at his next meeting of his contact with González Vega to provoke a reaction
from the LIRING establishment.

TRUCKDFER
MICROFILMED
DEC 12 1968
DCC. MICPO. SER.
i. Forwarded under separate cover is an issue of a
supposedly "literary" Cuban publication containing two short
essays by the Salvadorian poet and writer Roque DALTON.
The first of these essays is dedicated to LIRING-3. The
interesting thing is that LIRING-3 was at that time imprisoned
in Guatemala. The essay may thus be viewed as a tribute to
"a suffering supporter of the cause."
1
2. Roque DALTON (201-215097) is, according to the files
of the Station, an agent of the Cuban Intelligence Service
engaged in clandestine activities for the Communist Party of
El Salvador. DALTON spent some time in Czechoslovakia and is
now living in Cuba. He is the brother of Margarita DALTON
(201-751261), whom the Cuban IS recruited to work in Mexico.
LIRING-3 got to know DALTON in Havana in 1962-63 and became
a close friend of his (see HMMA-32283, 19 June 1967). DALTON
at one point confided to LIRING-3 that he had been approached
by WOFIRM while incarcerated in El Salvador.
3. The Station is hoping that DALTON's essay is an
indication that LIRING-3 is going to be viewed by the Cuban's
in much better light after his incarceration in Guatemala. 1
A report of LIRING-3's complete debriefing by ROWTON was
forwarded with HMMA-35904, 27 November 1968.

¿Que es
la Praxis?

Toda praxia en actividad, pero no toda
netividad es prusis. Al señalar Marx qua
el idealismo, en contraste con el materia-
lis:no, acimito el fudo netivo de la relación
sujeto-objeto, y al subrayar, a su vez, su

tlea-,(9) nos proviene contra todo intento
do establecer un signo de igualdad entro
uctividad y, praxis. De ahí que para deli-

y mu relación con otras neilyldudts, sea
preciso distinguir la praxis, como forma
de actividad pecifion, de otras que pue
dien estar indeo intimamente vliculadun
a ella.
Por actividad en general, entendemos
el acto o conjunto de actos en virtud do
los cunles un sujeto netivo (agente) mo-
difica una materia prima dadu.(e) Esta
carauterización do in nelivalud justamento
por su generalidad no experilica of tipo de
agente (fisico, biológies a humano) al la
naturaleza de la materia prima sobre la
que actúa (citerpo fisico, ser vivo, viven
cia psíquica, grupo, relación o institución
social) determina tampoco la e-poeio
de actos (fisicos, psíquicos, sociales) que
conducen u cierta trañi formación, El re-
stustadtɔ ɖo la nelivikud, a son, ku producto
so da usimilamo, en niveios diverkost pues
do ser una nuova particula, un concepto,
un útil, una obra artística o un nuevo sis®
toma social,
En esto amplio sentido, actividad se
opone a pusividad, y su osfera es la de la
efectividad, no la de lo meramente posl.
ble.
Agento es în quo obra, lo que actúa
y no lo que vath solemente en posibilidad
o disponibilidad de actuar u obrar. Su
actividad no es potencial, sino actual. Se
da eferlivamento sin que pueda ser sepa-
rada del acto o conjunto de actos que la
constituyen. La actividad muestra en las
rolaciones entre las partes y el todo los
rasgos de una totalldad concreta. Varios
actos desarticulados o yuxtapuestos¨ ca+
sualmente no permiten hablar de activi.
dad; es preciso que los actos singulares
so artiquien o estructuren, como elemen.
Om de un todo, o de un proceso total, quo
desemboca en la modificación de una ma-
teria prima. Por ello, a los actos del
agente y a la materia sobre la cual se
elerce esta actividad, hay que agregar el
resultado o prošiteto que es era 'materia
mirmu ya transformada por el agente.
Nuestro concepto de actividades to su
flejentemente amplio para que englobe,
por ejemplo: a un niyet fisico, las relacion
nes nucleares do determinadus particulas
que conducen a la transformación de unos
elementos quiinlens en u conjunto, o la

un nivel psíquico, îns actividades del hom.
bre o del animal del tipo de la sonsorial,
refleja Instintiva, etcétera; en este plano
instintivo, la actividad puedo manifestarse
como una serie de actos tan complejos
como el de la construcción de un nido por

minarse praxis social, aunque en un sene
tido ampllo toda práctica (incluyendo
aquella que tiene por objeto directo a la
naturaleza) reviste un carácter social, ya
que el hombre sólo puede llevarla a cabo
contrayendo determinadas relaciones so-
ciales (relaciones de producción en la
praxis productiva) y, además, porque la
modificación práctica del objeto no hura-
no se traduce, a su vez, en una transfor-
mación del hombre como ser social.
En un sentido más restringido, In pra-
xix social es la actividad de grupos o cla-
xes sociales que conduce a transformar In
organización y dirección de in sociedad, o
a realizar ciertos cambios mediante la uc-
tividad del Estado. Esta forma de praxis
es justamente la actividad politien.
En las condiciones de la sociedad divi-
dida en clases antagóniens, la politlea
comprende la fuchn du elusos por el poder
y la dirección y estructuración de la socie
dad, de acuerdo con los intereses y fines
corespondientes. La politica es una ac-
tividad prácties en cuanto que la lucha
que libran los grupos o clases sociales Ne
halla vinculada a cierto tipo de organiza-
clón real de sus miembros (ustituciones
y organizaciones politicas, como son, por
ejemplo, los partidos) en segundo lugar,
aunque la actividad politica vaya neom-
pañada de un choque y contraposición de
Idens, proyectos, programas, etcétera, y
exta lucha Ideológien ejerza una influenelių
indudable en las acciones politicas reales,
concretas, el carácter práctico de la neti.
vidad politien exige formas, medios y mé-
todos reales, efreíivos, de lucha; asi, por
ejemplo, el proietariado en su lucha poil-
tien se vale de huelgas, manifestaciónes,
mitiues e incluso de métodos violentos,
En tercer hugar, în netividad política gira
en torno a la conquista, conservación, dl-
rección o control do un organismo conere-
to como ex el Estado. El poder es un
Instrumento de importancia vital para la
transformación de in sociedad.
La praxis politica presupone la parti.
cipación de amplios sectores de la socie-
dad. Pero no se trata de una actividad
espontânea, aunque se den en ella scios
espontáneos de determinados individuos o
grupos. Persigue determinados fines que
responden a los intereses radicales de las
clases sociales, y en curta situnción còn.
creta la realización de esos fines se halla
1
condicionada por las posibilidades objeti-
vas inscritas en la propia realidad. Una
política que iesponda a esas posibilidades
y que excluya todo aventureiisino, exige
un conocimiento de esa realidad y de la
correlación de clases para no proponerse
acciones que desemboquen inexorablemen
te en un fracaro. La hicim tiene que ser,
por tanto, consciente, organizada y dirigi-
da, y la necesidad de librarla en esto forma
expilea la creación de los partidos poli- ·
ticos.
Los partidos trazan, con una mayor o
menor conciencia de los objetivos, post-
bilidades y condiciones, la linea de accion.
Los métodos para transion mar lo ideal en
real, es decir, para realizar prácticaniente
la linea politica trazada por un partido
constituye la estrategia y la táctica. La
estrategia señala las tarcas correspondien-
tes a una etapa historica general, y la
táctica determina el modo de cumplir la
lines politien de un periodo relativamente
brove. Estrategia y táctica se relacionan
dentro de la linea politica y de su aplica
ción como lo general y lo partieniar.
La' pruxis politica, en cuanto actividad
práctica transformadora, alcanza su for
ma más alta en la praxis revolucionaria
como einpa superior de la transformación
práctica de la sociedad, En in sociedad
dividida en clases antagónicas, la netividad
revolucionaria permite campiar radical-
mente las bases económicas y sociales en
que se asienta el poder material y e piri-
tual de la clase dominante, e instaurar asi
lina nueva sociedad. El agente principal
de este cambio es el proletariado a través
de una lucha conselente, organizada y diri-
gida, lo que presupone la existencia ɖɔ
!
un partido que eleve su conciencia de clasa
y trace claramente los objetivos do estil
jucha, su extrafezia y xùi tágtien, que orgu-
nice las fuerzas y las diriku,
Si el hombre existe en cuanto tal como
ser práctico, es decir; afirmandose con sù
actividad práctica transformadora frente
a la naturaleza exterior y fronte a su
propia naturaleza, la praxis revolucionarla
y la praxis productivă constitüyen doi di•
mensiones esenciales de su see prático.
Pero, a su vez, una y otra uclividad, junto
con Ins restantes formas específicas do
praxis, no son sino formas concretas par-

cias a la cual el hombre como ser social y
consciente humaniza los objetos y se hu-
maniza a si mismo.

proscrito. La primera no podia ya y el

LA PALMA
DE LA MANO
José Lezama Lima
La palma de la mano sobre el río.
La palma paso a paso, hacia mí, leyéndome.
Narciso mascado por la niebla ascendente,
vuelven los dioses descensores, Orfeo
y Stephanophorophoro.
El indice demuestra, señala la inflexible
Hanura de in nieve, demuestra.
El indice demuestra la carreta sobre un hllo,
la diagonal con cuerpo de cocodrilo
y cabeza de gavilán,
el anillo de oro en el tumor de la luna.
Ia mano se extiende sobre la llanura
de nieve, la palma de la mano
acompasa la boga del río.
La carreta conduce un canoso
reloj de pared. Icaro con dos guadañas.
Saturno se come las alas de corn.
Se extiende, demuestra, se deja leer.
learo, ya caldo, nadando,
habla con el Resucitado sentado en el légamo.
El vencido por el sol regresa con las estaciones
y el que triunfa de la muerte se vuelve a morir.
Es un bodegón de cebolla, manzana y amapolas.
El aira está exprimido en el puño
que se cierra, el arador por la palma de la mano
deja el reminiscente batido y batihojas,
el deseo paliducho, In scrpiente, el doble
del comienzo, el truchimán vindicativo,
eírculo que golpea en las narices.
La capota enída se mide por su sombra.
Icaro vencido y el Resucitado vencedor,
el Resucitado esperando la muerte
y el Icaro eterno relator.
En su sangre el laberinto y el torete
oscuro luchando con el tigre dormido.
